I found the key issue. Look at the `loadMailDetails` function (lines 397-408):\n\nFor non-legacy mails (lines 402-406):\n```typescript\nconst mailDetailsId = neverNull(mail.mailDetails)\nreturn entityClient\n    .loadMultiple(MailDetailsBlobTypeRef, listIdPart(mailDetailsId), [elementIdPart(mailDetailsId)])\n    .then((d) => MailWrapper.details(mail, d[0].details))\n```\n\nThe function calls `entityClient.loadMultiple()` without passing any session key information! The `mail` object has the session key available (in `mail._ownerEncSessionKey` or via the encryption key), but this is not being passed to the `loadMultiple` method.\n\nWhen `loadMultiple` is called, it internally calls `_handleLoadMultipleResult` which calls `_decryptMapAndMigrate` for each entity. The `_decryptMapAndMigrate` method tries to resolve the session key from the raw entity itself:\n\n```typescript\nasync _decryptMapAndMigrate<T>(instance: any, model: TypeModel): Promise<T> {\n    let sessionKey\n    try {\n        sessionKey = await this._crypto.resolveSessionKey(model, instance)  // <-- NO OWNERKEY PARAMETER\n    } catch (e) {\n        ...\n    }\n    const decryptedInstance = await this.instanceMapper.decryptAndMapToInstance<T>(model, instance, sessionKey)\n    ...\n}\n```\n\nThe problem is that when the entity is loaded via `loadMultiple`, it doesn't have the owner's session key in it. The session key is encrypted with the owner's encryption key. For non-legacy mails with the new permission model, the session key isn't stored in the entity itself - it's stored in the parent mail object.\n\nThis is the bug! The `loadMailDetails` function should pass the session key from the `mail` object to the `loadMultiple` call, but there's no way to do that with the current API.\n\n\nThe same pattern likely appears
